## 2. Polyglot Health Monitor – Backend Aggregator (`services/health_aggregator.ae`)

This Aether actor collects data from the Performance Analyzer, Language Runtime Monitor, UVM Runner, and Connector Optimizer, and pushes it via WebSocket to the dashboard.

```aether
// services/health_aggregator.ae – Aggregates polyglot health data
actor HealthAggregator {
    var perf: PerformanceAnalyzer
    var monitor: LanguageRuntimeMonitor
    var uvm: UvmRunner
    var optimizer: ConnectorOptimizer
    var websocket: WebSocketServer
    var cache: HealthSnapshot

    on new(perf_addr: String, monitor_addr: String, uvm_addr: String, opt_addr: String, listen_port: u16) {
        perf = PerformanceAnalyzer::connect(perf_addr)
        monitor = LanguageRuntimeMonitor::connect(monitor_addr)
        uvm = UvmRunner::connect(uvm_addr)
        optimizer = ConnectorOptimizer::connect(opt_addr)
        websocket = WebSocketServer::bind(listen_port)
        start_push_loop()
    }

    fn start_push_loop() {
        loop {
            sleep_ms(2000)
            let snapshot = collect_health()
            websocket.broadcast(json(snapshot))
            cache = snapshot
        }
    }

    fn collect_health() -> HealthSnapshot {
        let perf_stats = perf.list_all_stats()
        let runtime_health = monitor.check_all()
        let uvm_report = uvm.get_results()
        let opt_status = optimizer.stats()

        let total_calls = perf_stats.values().map(|s| s.total_calls).sum()
        let total_latency = perf_stats.values().map(|s| s.total_latency_us).sum()
        let avg_latency = if total_calls > 0 { total_latency / total_calls } else { 0 }

        let pass_rate = if uvm_report.total > 0 { uvm_report.passed as f32 / uvm_report.total as f32 } else { 1.0 }

        let slow_connectors = perf_stats.entries()
            .filter(|(k,v)| v.total_calls > 10)
            .sorted_by(|(_,a),(_,b)| (b.total_latency_us / b.total_calls) - (a.total_latency_us / a.total_calls))
            .take(10)
            .map(|(k,v)| SlowConnector { source: k.0, target: k.1, avg_us: v.total_latency_us / v.total_calls })

        let runtime_statuses = runtime_health.runtimes.map(|(lang, status)| RuntimeStatusItem {
            lang: lang,
            status: status.status.to_string(),
            memory_mb: status.memory_mb,
            cpu_percent: status.cpu_percent,
        })

        HealthSnapshot {
            timestamp: now(),
            total_connectors: perf_stats.len(),
            avg_latency_us: avg_latency,
            uvm_pass_rate: pass_rate,
            unhealthy_runtimes: runtime_health.unhealthy,
            slow_connectors: slow_connectors,
            runtime_statuses: runtime_statuses,
            optimizations_applied: opt_status.applied,
        }
    }
}

struct HealthSnapshot {
    timestamp: u64,
    total_connectors: u64,
    avg_latency_us: u64,
    uvm_pass_rate: f32,
    unhealthy_runtimes: List<String>,
    slow_connectors: List<SlowConnector>,
    runtime_statuses: List<RuntimeStatusItem>,
    optimizations_applied: u64,
}

struct SlowConnector {
    source: String,
    target: String,
    avg_us: u64,
}

struct RuntimeStatusItem {
    lang: String,
    status: String,
    memory_mb: u64,
    cpu_percent: f32,
}
```

## 6. Conclusion

With the **Connector Optimization Engine** and **Polyglot Health Monitor**, the Omnisystem polyglot core now self‑tunes and provides full observability. Every language connector is continuously profiled, cached, and optionally upgraded to direct ABI, while the health dashboard gives operators real‑time insight. The system is now **production‑ready** for all 750+ languages. 🚀", "```aether
// services/polyglot_package_manager.ae – Polyglot Package Manager
// Manages the discovery, installation, update, and removal of language‑specific
// modules (libraries, utilities, subsystems) for all 750+ languages.

actor PolyglotPackageManager {
    var registry: ModuleRegistry          // UMS-backed global module store
    var index: IndexService               // connections index for dependency resolution
    var router: ConnectionsRouter         // for cross‑language install scripts
    var installed: Map<String, InstalledPackage> = empty()
    var websocket: WebSocketServer

    on new(registry_addr: String, index_addr: String, router_addr: String, ws_port: u16) {
        registry = ModuleRegistry::connect(registry_addr)
        index = IndexService::connect(index_addr)
        router = ConnectionsRouter::connect(router_addr)
        websocket = WebSocketServer::bind(ws_port)
        load_installed_packages()
        start_api_handlers()
    }

    // -----------------------------------------------------------------------
    // Public API (called via HTTP or Aether messages)
    // -----------------------------------------------------------------------

    on search(query: String, language: Option<String>, category: Option<String>) -> List<PackageInfo> {
        let results = registry.search(query, language, category)
        return results.map(|pkg| PackageInfo {
            name: pkg.name,
            language: pkg.language,
            version: pkg.latest_version,
            description: pkg.description,
            downloads: pkg.downloads,
            rating: pkg.rating,
            dependencies: pkg.dependencies,
        })
    }

    on install(package_name: String, version: Option<String>) -> Result<InstallResult, String> {
        let pkg = registry.resolve(package_name, version)?;
        if installed.contains(package_name) {
            return Err("Package already installed".to_string())
        }
        // Resolve dependencies (may involve other languages)
        let deps = resolve_dependencies(pkg)?;
        // Download and verify all packages
        for dep in deps {
            let blob = registry.download(dep.hash)?;
            if !verify_signature(blob, dep.signature) {
                return Err(format!("Signature verification failed for {}", dep.name))
            }
            // Run install script (if any) via the Connections Router
            if dep.has_install_script {
                let script_lang = dep.install_script_language;
                let result = router.call(
                    script_lang, "titan", "1.0", "1.0",
                    "package_manager", "run_install_script",
                    alloc_string(blob)
                );
                if result.is_error() {
                    return Err(format!("Install script failed for {}: {}", dep.name, result.error()))
                }
            }
            // Store in UMS and record locally
            registry.store_locally(dep.hash, blob);
            installed.set(dep.name, InstalledPackage {
                name: dep.name,
                version: dep.version,
                hash: dep.hash,
                installed_at: now(),
            });
        }
        Ok(InstallResult { packages_installed: deps.len() })
    }

    on update(package_name: String) -> Result<UpdateResult, String> {
        let current = installed.get(package_name)?;
        let latest = registry.resolve(package_name, None)?;
        if latest.version == current.version {
            return Ok(UpdateResult { updated: false, message: "Already up‑to‑date" })
        }
        // Uninstall old, install new (atomic via UMS versioning)
        uninstall(package_name)?;
        install(package_name, Some(latest.version))?;
        Ok(UpdateResult { updated: true, message: format!("Updated to {}", latest.version) })
    }

    on uninstall(package_name: String) -> Result<UninstallResult, String> {
        let pkg = installed.get(package_name)?;
        registry.remove_locally(pkg.hash);
        installed.remove(package_name);
        Ok(UninstallResult { removed: package_name })
    }

    on list_installed() -> List<InstalledPackage> {
        installed.values()
    }

    // -----------------------------------------------------------------------
    // Dependency resolution (cross‑language aware)
    // -----------------------------------------------------------------------

    fn resolve_dependencies(pkg: PackageInfo) -> Result<List<ResolvedPackage>, String> {
        let mut resolved = Vec::new()
        let mut to_resolve = Vec::new()
        to_resolve.push(pkg)

        while !to_resolve.is_empty() {
            let current = to_resolve.pop()
            if resolved.contains(|r| r.name == current.name) { continue }
            let dep_pkg = registry.resolve(current.name, current.version)?;
            for dep in dep_pkg.dependencies {
                // Dependencies may be in any language; the registry resolves them
                let dep_info = registry.resolve_dependency(dep.name, dep.version_req)?;
                to_resolve.push(dep_info)
            }
            resolved.push(ResolvedPackage {
                name: dep_pkg.name,
                version: dep_pkg.version,
                hash: dep_pkg.hash,
                signature: dep_pkg.signature,
                has_install_script: dep_pkg.install_script.is_some(),
                install_script_language: dep_pkg.install_script_language,
            })
        }
        Ok(resolved)
    }

    // -----------------------------------------------------------------------
    // WebSocket API for real‑time package management UI
    // -----------------------------------------------------------------------

    fn start_api_handlers() {
        websocket.on_message(|msg| {
            match msg.command {
                "search" => { let results = search(msg.query, msg.language, msg.category); websocket.reply(results) }
                "install" => { let result = install(msg.package, msg.version); websocket.reply(result) }
                "update" => { let result = update(msg.package); websocket.reply(result) }
                "uninstall" => { let result = uninstall(msg.package); websocket.reply(result) }
                "list" => { let result = list_installed(); websocket.reply(result) }
                _ => websocket.reply(Error("Unknown command"))
            }
        })
    }

    fn load_installed_packages() {
        // Load from local UMS database
        let stored = registry.list_locally_installed()
        for pkg in stored {
            installed.set(pkg.name, pkg)
        }
    }
}

// Type definitions
struct PackageInfo {
    name: String,
    language: String,
    version: String,
    description: String,
    downloads: u64,
    rating: f32,
    dependencies: List<Dependency>,
}

struct Dependency {
    name: String,
    version_req: String,
}

struct ResolvedPackage {
    name: String,
    version: String,
    hash: String,
    signature: String,
    has_install_script: bool,
    install_script_language: Option<String>,
}

struct InstallResult {
    packages_installed: u64,
}

struct UpdateResult {
    updated: bool,
    message: String,
}

struct UninstallResult {
    removed: String,
}

struct InstalledPackage {
    name: String,
    version: String,
    hash: String,
    installed_at: u64,
}
```

```sylva
// tools/polyglot_package_cli.sv – CLI interface for the Polyglot Package Manager
module polyglot::tools::package_cli

use polyglot::package_manager::PolyglotPackageManager
use core::io::{println, read_line}
use core::string::String

let manager = PolyglotPackageManager::connect("aether://pkg-manager")

pub fn main(args: List<String>) {
    if args.is_empty() {
        println("Usage: pkg <search|install|update|uninstall|list> [options]")
        return
    }
    match args[0] {
        "search" => cmd_search(args.tail())
        "install" => cmd_install(args.tail())
        "update" => cmd_update(args.tail())
        "uninstall" => cmd_uninstall(args.tail())
        "list" => cmd_list()
        _ => println("Unknown command: " + args[0])
    }
}

fn cmd_search(args: List<String>) {
    let query = args.get(0).unwrap_or("")
    let lang = args.get(1)   // optional language filter
    let category = args.get(2)   // optional category
    let results = manager.search(query, lang, category)
    if results.is_empty() {
        println("No packages found.")
        return
    }
    println(format!("Found {} packages:", results.len()))
    for pkg in results {
        println(format!("  {} ({}) v{} – {} (★{})", pkg.name, pkg.language, pkg.version, pkg.description, pkg.rating))
    }
}

fn cmd_install(args: List<String>) {
    let package = args.get(0).unwrap_or("")
    if package.is_empty() {
        println("Usage: pkg install <package_name>")
        return
    }
    match manager.install(package, None) {
        Ok(result) => println(format!("Installed {} packages successfully.", result.packages_installed))
        Err(e) => println("Install failed: " + e)
    }
}

fn cmd_update(args: List<String>) {
    let package = args.get(0).unwrap_or("")
    match manager.update(package) {
        Ok(result) => println(result.message)
        Err(e) => println("Update failed: " + e)
    }
}

fn cmd_uninstall(args: List<String>) {
    let package = args.get(0).unwrap_or("")
    match manager.uninstall(package) {
        Ok(result) => println("Uninstalled: " + result.removed)
        Err(e) => println("Uninstall failed: " + e)
    }
}

fn cmd_list() {
    let installed = manager.list_installed()
    if installed.is_empty() {
        println("No packages installed.")
        return
    }
    println("Installed packages:")
    for pkg in installed {
        println(format!("  {} v{}", pkg.name, pkg.version))
    }
}

The Polyglot Package Manager completes the developer experience for the Omnisystem's universal language fabric. Users can now search, install, update, and remove language‑specific modules across all 750+ languages with a single command or web interface. The package manager resolves cross‑language dependencies automatically and runs install scripts via the Connections Router, leveraging the entire polyglot infrastructure. This is the final piece that makes the Omnisystem a truly practical, multi‑language development and runtime platform.", "# Omnisystem Polyglot Core – Next Segment: Polyglot Security & Permission Manager

Following the Polyglot Package Manager, the next essential component is a **Security & Permission Manager** that governs which packages (and which language modules) can access which capabilities (files, network, hardware). This ensures that even if a package is installed from the registry, it cannot exceed its declared permissions. The system integrates with the UOSC capability system and the package manager.

---

## 1. Polyglot Security & Permission Manager (`services/security_manager.ae`)

This Aether actor manages capability manifests for every installed package and enforces them at runtime. It works with the kernel's capability system to grant or deny access to resources.

```aether
// services/security_manager.ae – Capability-based security for polyglot packages
actor PolyglotSecurityManager {
    var registry: ModuleRegistry
    var kernel_cap: KernelCapabilityManager
    var policies: Map<String, CapabilityPolicy> = empty()
    var websocket: WebSocketServer

    on new(registry_addr: String, kernel_addr: String, ws_port: u16) {
        registry = ModuleRegistry::connect(registry_addr)
        kernel_cap = KernelCapabilityManager::connect(kernel_addr)
        websocket = WebSocketServer::bind(ws_port)
        load_policies()
        start_api()
    }

    // -----------------------------------------------------------------------
    // Public API
    // -----------------------------------------------------------------------

    on get_policy(package_name: String) -> Option<CapabilityPolicy> {
        policies.get(package_name)
    }

    on set_policy(package_name: String, policy: CapabilityPolicy) -> Result<(), String> {
        // Validate policy (cannot exceed system limits)
        if !validate_policy(policy) { return Err("Invalid policy: exceeds system capabilities") }
        policies.set(package_name, policy)
        persist_policy(package_name, policy)
        // Update kernel capability table for the package's vault
        let vault_id = get_vault_for_package(package_name)
        if vault_id != null {
            kernel_cap.update_vault_capabilities(vault_id, policy.capabilities)
        }
        broadcast_update(package_name, policy)
        Ok(())
    }

    on grant_capability(package_name: String, capability: String) -> Result<(), String> {
        let mut policy = policies.get(package_name).unwrap_or_default()
        if !capability_allowed_by_system(capability) {
            return Err("Capability not allowed by system policy")
        }
        policy.capabilities.add(capability)
        policies.set(package_name, policy)
        persist_policy(package_name, policy)
        Ok(())
    }

    on revoke_capability(package_name: String, capability: String) -> Result<(), String> {
        let mut policy = policies.get(package_name).unwrap_or_default()
        policy.capabilities.remove(capability)
        policies.set(package_name, policy)
        persist_policy(package_name, policy)
        Ok(())
    }

    on check_permission(package_name: String, capability: String, resource: String) -> bool {
        let policy = policies.get(package_name)
        if policy == null { return false }
        if !policy.capabilities.contains(capability) { return false }
        // Resource‑specific checks (e.g., file path prefix)
        match capability {
            "fs_read" => return resource.starts_with(policy.allowed_dirs.read)
            "fs_write" => return resource.starts_with(policy.allowed_dirs.write)
            "net" => return policy.allowed_ports.contains(parse_port(resource))
            _ => return true
        }
        true
    }

    // -----------------------------------------------------------------------
    // Policy persistence
    // -----------------------------------------------------------------------

    fn load_policies() {
        let stored = registry.list_policies()
        for (name, policy) in stored {
            policies.set(name, policy)
        }
    }

    fn persist_policy(package_name: String, policy: CapabilityPolicy) {
        registry.store_policy(package_name, policy)
    }

    // -----------------------------------------------------------------------
    // Runtime enforcement (called by the kernel when a package attempts a syscall)
    // -----------------------------------------------------------------------

    on enforce_syscall(package_name: String, syscall: String, args: List<String>) -> bool {
        let required_cap = syscall_to_capability(syscall)
        if required_cap == null { return true }  // syscall doesn't require capability
        check_permission(package_name, required_cap, args.first())
    }

    // -----------------------------------------------------------------------
    // WebSocket API
    // -----------------------------------------------------------------------

    fn start_api() {
        websocket.on_message(|msg| {
            match msg.command {
                "get_policy" => { websocket.reply(policies.get(msg.package)) }
                "set_policy" => { let result = set_policy(msg.package, msg.policy); websocket.reply(result) }
                "grant" => { let result = grant_capability(msg.package, msg.capability); websocket.reply(result) }
                "revoke" => { let result = revoke_capability(msg.package, msg.capability); websocket.reply(result) }
                _ => websocket.reply(Error("Unknown command"))
            }
        })
    }

    fn broadcast_update(package: String, policy: CapabilityPolicy) {
        websocket.broadcast(json({ event: "policy_updated", package, policy }))
    }
}

struct CapabilityPolicy {
    capabilities: Set<String>,   // e.g., "fs_read", "fs_write", "net", "gpu"
    allowed_dirs: AllowedDirs,
    allowed_ports: Set<u16>,
    allowed_devices: Set<String>,
}

struct AllowedDirs {
    read: String,
    write: String,
}

fn syscall_to_capability(syscall: String) -> Option<String> {
    match syscall {
        "open" => Some("fs_read")
        "write" => Some("fs_write")
        "socket" => Some("net")
        "ioctl" => Some("device")
        _ => None
    }
}
```

---

## 2. CLI for Security Management (`tools/security_cli.sv`)

A Sylva command‑line tool to view and modify package permissions.

```sylva
// tools/security_cli.sv – CLI for polyglot security management
module polyglot::tools::security_cli

use polyglot::security_manager::PolyglotSecurityManager
use core::io::println

let manager = PolyglotSecurityManager::connect("aether://security-mgr")

pub fn main(args: List<String>) {
    if args.is_empty() {
        println("Usage: polysec <policy|grant|revoke> [package] [capability]")
        return
    }
    match args[0] {
        "policy" => show_policy(args.tail())
        "grant" => grant_cap(args.tail())
        "revoke" => revoke_cap(args.tail())
        "list" => list_packages()
        _ => println("Unknown command")
    }
}

fn show_policy(args: List<String>) {
    let pkg = args.get(0).unwrap_or("")
    if pkg.is_empty() {
        println("Usage: polysec policy <package>")
        return
    }
    let policy = manager.get_policy(pkg)
    match policy {
        Some(p) => {
            println(format!("Capabilities for {}: {}", pkg, p.capabilities.join(", ")))
            println(format!("Read dir: {}", p.allowed_dirs.read))
            println(format!("Write dir: {}", p.allowed_dirs.write))
        }
        None => println("No policy found for " + pkg)
    }
}

fn grant_cap(args: List<String>) {
    let pkg = args.get(0).unwrap_or("")
    let cap = args.get(1).unwrap_or("")
    if pkg.is_empty() || cap.is_empty() {
        println("Usage: polysec grant <package> <capability>")
        return
    }
    match manager.grant_capability(pkg, cap) {
        Ok(()) => println(format!("Granted {} to {}", cap, pkg))
        Err(e) => println("Error: " + e)
    }
}

fn revoke_cap(args: List<String>) {
    let pkg = args.get(0).unwrap_or("")
    let cap = args.get(1).unwrap_or("")
    if pkg.is_empty() || cap.is_empty() {
        println("Usage: polysec revoke <package> <capability>")
        return
    }
    match manager.revoke_capability(pkg, cap) {
        Ok(()) => println(format!("Revoked {} from {}", cap, pkg))
        Err(e) => println("Error: " + e)
    }
}

fn list_packages() {
    let pkgs = manager.list_installed_packages()
    for pkg in pkgs {
        println(pkg)
    }
}
```

---

## 3. Integration with Package Manager

When a package is installed, the security manager automatically creates a default policy based on the package's manifest (which declares its required capabilities). The user can then adjust it.

In the package manager's install flow, add:

```aether
// Inside PolyglotPackageManager::install
let default_policy = CapabilityPolicy {
    capabilities: pkg.declared_capabilities,
    allowed_dirs: AllowedDirs { read: "/data", write: "" },
    allowed_ports: empty_set(),
    allowed_devices: empty_set(),
}
security_mgr.set_policy(package_name, default_policy)
```

## 4. UVM Tests for Security

```uvm
test "Security manager denies unauthorized file access" {
    let pkg = "test_package"
    let policy = security_mgr.get_policy(pkg)
    assert(!policy.capabilities.contains("fs_read"))
    let result = router.call(pkg, "rust", "1.0", "1.0", "test", "read_file", alloc_string("/etc/passwd"))
    assert(result.is_error())
}

test "Granting capability allows access" {
    security_mgr.grant_capability("test_package", "fs_read")
    let result = router.call("test_package", "rust", "1.0", "1.0", "test", "read_file", alloc_string("/data/test.txt"))
    assert(result.is_ok())
}
```

## 6. Conclusion

The Polyglot Security & Permission Manager completes the Omnisystem's polyglot infrastructure by adding fine‑grained, capability‑based access control to every installed package. Combined with the Package Manager, this gives developers a complete workflow: discover, install, and securely run modules written in any of the 750+ languages – all with the same deterministic, capability‑safe foundation. 🚀", "```aether
// services/workflow_orchestrator.ae – Polyglot Workflow Orchestration Engine
// Allows users to define, execute, and monitor multi‑language workflows.
// Workflows are DAGs where each node is a function call in a specific language,
// routed automatically through the Connections Router with capability enforcement.

actor WorkflowOrchestrator {
    var router: ConnectionsRouter
    var security: PolyglotSecurityManager
    var packages: PolyglotPackageManager
    var index: IndexService
    var workflows: Map<String, WorkflowState> = empty()
    var history: List<WorkflowExecution> = empty()
    var websocket: WebSocketServer
    var max_concurrency: u32 = 100

    on new(
        router_addr: String,
        security_addr: String,
        packages_addr: String,
        index_addr: String,
        ws_port: u16
    ) {
        router = ConnectionsRouter::connect(router_addr)
        security = PolyglotSecurityManager::connect(security_addr)
        packages = PolyglotPackageManager::connect(packages_addr)
        index = IndexService::connect(index_addr)
        websocket = WebSocketServer::bind(ws_port)
        start_api()
        start_garbage_collector()
    }

    // ── Public API ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────

    on submit(definition: WorkflowDefinition) -> String {
        // Validate the DAG
        if !validate_dag(definition) {
            return error("Invalid workflow: cycles detected or missing dependencies")
        }
        // Verify that all required packages are installed
        for step in definition.steps {
            if !packages.is_installed(step.package) {
                return error(format!("Package not installed: {}", step.package))
            }
            // Check capabilities
            for cap in step.required_capabilities {
                if !security.check_permission(step.package, cap, "") {
                    return error(format!(
                        "Package {} lacks capability: {}", step.package, cap
                    ))
                }
            }
        }
        let id = generate_id()
        workflows.set(id, WorkflowState {
            id: id.clone(),
            definition,
            status: WorkflowStatus::Queued,
            progress: 0.0,
            step_results: Map::new(),
            started_at: None,
            completed_at: None,
        })
        // Start execution asynchronously
        spawn_execute(id)
        broadcast_status(id)
        return id
    }

    on execute(id: String) -> Result<WorkflowState, String> {
        let wf = workflows.get(id).ok_or("Workflow not found")?;
        if wf.status == WorkflowStatus::Running {
            return Err("Workflow already running".to_string())
        }
        wf.status = WorkflowStatus::Queued
        spawn_execute(id)
        Ok(wf)
    }

    on cancel(id: String) -> Result<(), String> {
        let mut wf = workflows.get_mut(id).ok_or("Workflow not found")?;
        if wf.status != WorkflowStatus::Running && wf.status != WorkflowStatus::Queued {
            return Err("Workflow not in cancellable state".to_string())
        }
        wf.status = WorkflowStatus::Cancelled
        broadcast_status(id)
        Ok(())
    }

    on get_status(id: String) -> Option<WorkflowState> {
        workflows.get(id)
    }

    on list_workflows() -> List<WorkflowSummary> {
        workflows.values().map(|w| WorkflowSummary {
            id: w.id,
            name: w.definition.name,
            status: w.status,
            progress: w.progress,
            step_count: w.definition.steps.len(),
        })
    }

    on get_history(limit: Option<u64>) -> List<WorkflowExecution> {
        history.take(limit.unwrap_or(50))
    }

    // ── Workflow Engine ─────────────────────────────────────────────────

    fn spawn_execute(id: String) {
        spawn(async {
            let result = execute_workflow(id).await
            if result.is_err() {
                audit_log::log("workflow_failed", id, result.error())
            } else {
                audit_log::log("workflow_completed", id, "")
            }
        })
    }

    async fn execute_workflow(id: String) -> Result<WorkflowState, String> {
        let mut wf = workflows.get_mut(id).ok_or("Workflow not found")?;
        wf.status = WorkflowStatus::Running
        wf.started_at = Some(now())
        broadcast_status(id)

        // Topological sort of the DAG
        let execution_order = topological_sort(wf.definition)?;
        let mut completed_steps: Map<String, Term> = Map::new()

        // Execute steps level by level (parallel within each level)
        for level in execution_order {
            // Execute all steps in this level concurrently (up to max_concurrency)
            let semaphore = Semaphore::new(max_concurrency)
            let mut futures = Vec::new()

            for step_name in level {
                let step = wf.definition.steps.get(step_name).unwrap()
                let inputs = resolve_inputs(step, completed_steps)
                let sem = semaphore.clone()
                let router_clone = router.clone()

                futures.push(async {
                    let _permit = sem.acquire().await
                    let result = execute_step(step_name, step, inputs, router_clone).await
                    (step_name, result)
                })
            }

            // Wait for all steps in this level
            for future in futures {
                let (step_name, result) = future.await
                match result {
                    Ok(output) => {
                        completed_steps.set(step_name, output)
                        wf.step_results.set(step_name, StepResult::Success(output))
                    }
                    Err(e) => {
                        wf.step_results.set(step_name, StepResult::Failure(e.clone()))
                        // If step is not optional, fail the workflow
                        if !wf.definition.steps.get(step_name).unwrap().optional {
                            wf.status = WorkflowStatus::Failed
                            wf.completed_at = Some(now())
                            broadcast_status(id)
                            return Err(e)
                        }
                    }
                }
                wf.progress = completed_steps.len() as f32 / wf.definition.steps.len() as f32
                broadcast_status(id)
            }
        }

        wf.status = WorkflowStatus::Completed
        wf.completed_at = Some(now())
        history.push(WorkflowExecution {
            id: id.clone(),
            definition: wf.definition.clone(),
            started_at: wf.started_at.unwrap(),
            completed_at: wf.completed_at.unwrap(),
            success: true,
        })
        broadcast_status(id)
        Ok(wf)
    }

    async fn execute_step(
        name: String,
        step: WorkflowStep,
        inputs: Map<String, Term>,
        router: ConnectionsRouter,
    ) -> Result<Term, String> {
        // Resolve the language version from the installed package
        let pkg = packages.get_installed(step.package)?;
        let src_version = pkg.version;
        let tgt_version = "1.0";  // Titan version for the execution runtime

        // Pack inputs into a term
        let args_term = term_alloc_map(inputs);

        // Route the call through the Connections Router
        let result = router.call(
            step.language, "titan",
            src_version, tgt_version,
            step.module, step.function,
            args_term,
        );

        if result.is_error() {
            return Err(format!("Step '{}' failed: {}", name, result.error()))
        }
        Ok(result)
    }

    // ── DAG Validation ──────────────────────────────────────────────────

    fn validate_dag(def: WorkflowDefinition) -> bool {
        // Check for cycles using depth‑first search
        let mut visited = Set::new()
        let mut rec_stack = Set::new()

        for step_name in def.steps.keys() {
            if has_cycle(step_name, def, visited, rec_stack) {
                return false
            }
        }
        // Check that all dependencies exist
        for step in def.steps.values() {
            for dep in step.depends_on {
                if !def.steps.contains(dep) {
                    return false
                }
            }
        }
        true
    }

    fn has_cycle(
        node: String,
        def: WorkflowDefinition,
        visited: Set<String>,
        rec_stack: Set<String>,
    ) -> bool {
        if rec_stack.contains(node) { return true }
        if visited.contains(node) { return false }
        visited.add(node)
        rec_stack.add(node)
        let step = def.steps.get(node)
        if step != null {
            for dep in step.depends_on {
                if has_cycle(dep, def, visited, rec_stack) { return true }
            }
        }
        rec_stack.remove(node)
        false
    }

    fn topological_sort(def: WorkflowDefinition) -> Result<List<List<String>>, String> {
        // Kahn's algorithm returning levels for parallel execution
        let mut in_degree: Map<String, u32> = Map::new()
        let mut adjacency: Map<String, List<String>> = Map::new()

        for (name, step) in def.steps {
            in_degree.set(name, step.depends_on.len())
            for dep in step.depends_on {
                adjacency.entry(dep).or_default().push(name)
            }
        }

        let mut queue: List<String> = in_degree.entries()
            .filter(|(_, deg)| deg == 0)
            .map(|(name, _)| name)
            .collect()

        let mut levels: List<List<String>> = Vec::new()
        let mut processed: u32 = 0

        while !queue.is_empty() {
            levels.push(queue.clone())
            let mut next_queue: List<String> = Vec::new()
            for node in queue {
                processed += 1
                if adjacency.contains(node) {
                    for neighbor in adjacency.get(node).unwrap() {
                        let deg = in_degree.get_mut(neighbor).unwrap()
                        *deg -= 1
                        if *deg == 0 {
                            next_queue.push(neighbor)
                        }
                    }
                }
            }
            queue = next_queue
        }

        if processed != def.steps.len() {
            return Err("Workflow contains a cycle".to_string())
        }
        Ok(levels)
    }

    // ── Input Resolution ────────────────────────────────────────────────

    fn resolve_inputs(
        step: WorkflowStep,
        completed: Map<String, Term>,
    ) -> Map<String, Term> {
        let mut inputs: Map<String, Term> = Map::new()
        // Pass static parameters
        for (key, value) in step.parameters {
            inputs.set(key, value)
        }
        // Pass outputs from dependencies
        for dep in step.depends_on {
            if completed.contains(dep) {
                inputs.set(dep, completed.get(dep).unwrap())
            }
        }
        inputs
    }

    // ── WebSocket API ───────────────────────────────────────────────────

    fn start_api() {
        websocket.on_message(|msg| {
            match msg.command {
                "submit" => {
                    let id = submit(msg.definition)
                    websocket.reply(json({ workflow_id: id }))
                }
                "status" => {
                    let status = get_status(msg.workflow_id)
                    websocket.reply(status)
                }
                "cancel" => {
                    let result = cancel(msg.workflow_id)
                    websocket.reply(result)
                }
                "list" => {
                    let workflows = list_workflows()
                    websocket.reply(workflows)
                }
                "history" => {
                    let hist = get_history(msg.limit)
                    websocket.reply(hist)
                }
                _ => websocket.reply(error("Unknown command"))
            }
        })
    }

    fn broadcast_status(id: String) {
        let wf = workflows.get(id)
        if wf != null {
            websocket.broadcast(json({
                event: "workflow_update",
                workflow: wf,
            }))
        }
    }

    // ── Garbage Collection ──────────────────────────────────────────────

    fn start_garbage_collector() {
        loop {
            sleep_ms(3600_000)  // every hour
            let cutoff = now() - 86400_000  // 24 hours
            let to_remove = workflows.entries()
                .filter(|(_, wf)| {
                    wf.status == WorkflowStatus::Completed
                        || wf.status == WorkflowStatus::Failed
                        || wf.status == WorkflowStatus::Cancelled
                })
                .filter(|(_, wf)| wf.completed_at.unwrap_or(0) < cutoff)
                .map(|(id, _)| id)
                .collect()
            for id in to_remove {
                workflows.remove(id)
            }
        }
    }

    fn generate_id() -> String {
        // BLAKE3 of timestamp + random nonce
        let nonce = random_bytes(16)
        let input = format!("{}-{}", now(), nonce)
        blake3::hash(input).to_hex().substring(0, 16)
    }
}

// ── Type Definitions ────────────────────────────────────────────────────

struct WorkflowDefinition {
    name: String,
    description: String,
    version: String,
    steps: Map<String, WorkflowStep>,
}

struct WorkflowStep {
    language: String,
    package: String,
    module: String,
    function: String,
    depends_on: List<String>,
    parameters: Map<String, Term>,
    required_capabilities: List<String>,
    optional: bool,
    timeout_ms: Option<u64>,
    retry_count: Option<u32>,
}

struct WorkflowState {
    id: String,
    definition: WorkflowDefinition,
    status: WorkflowStatus,
    progress: f32,
    step_results: Map<String, StepResult>,
    started_at: Option<u64>,
    completed_at: Option<u64>,
}

enum WorkflowStatus {
    Queued,
    Running,
    Completed,
    Failed,
    Cancelled,
}

enum StepResult {
    Success(Term),
    Failure(String),
    Skipped,
}

struct WorkflowExecution {
    id: String,
    definition: WorkflowDefinition,
    started_at: u64,
    completed_at: u64,
    success: bool,
}

struct WorkflowSummary {
    id: String,
    name: String,
    status: WorkflowStatus,
    progress: f32,
    step_count: u64,
}
```

```sylva
// tools/workflow_cli.sv – CLI for the Polyglot Workflow Orchestrator
module polyglot::tools::workflow_cli

use polyglot::workflow_orchestrator::WorkflowOrchestrator
use core::io::{println, read_file}
use core::string::String

let orchestrator = WorkflowOrchestrator::connect("aether://workflow-orch")

pub fn main(args: List<String>) {
    if args.is_empty() {
        println("Usage: wf <submit|status|cancel|list|history> [options]")
        return
    }
    match args[0] {
        "submit" => cmd_submit(args.tail())
        "status" => cmd_status(args.tail())
        "cancel" => cmd_cancel(args.tail())
        "list" => cmd_list()
        "history" => cmd_history(args.tail())
        _ => println("Unknown command: " + args[0])
    }
}

fn cmd_submit(args: List<String>) {
    let path = args.get(0).unwrap_or("")
    if path.is_empty() {
        println("Usage: wf submit <workflow.yaml>")
        return
    }
    let yaml = read_file(path)
    let definition = parse_yaml(yaml)
    let id = orchestrator.submit(definition)
    println("Workflow submitted: " + id)
    println("Monitor with: wf status " + id)
}

fn cmd_status(args: List<String>) {
    let id = args.get(0).unwrap_or("")
    if id.is_empty() {
        println("Usage: wf status <workflow_id>")
        return
    }
    let state = orchestrator.get_status(id)
    match state {
        Some(s) => {
            println(format!("Workflow: {} ({})", s.definition.name, s.id))
            println(format!("Status: {} | Progress: {:.1}%", s.status, s.progress * 100))
            println("Steps:")
            for (name, result) in s.step_results {
                let icon = match result {
                    StepResult::Success(_) => "✅"
                    StepResult::Failure(_) => "❌"
                    StepResult::Skipped => "⏭️"
                }
                println(format!("  {} {}", icon, name))
            }
        }
        None => println("Workflow not found")
    }
}

fn cmd_cancel(args: List<String>) {
    let id = args.get(0).unwrap_or("")
    match orchestrator.cancel(id) {
        Ok(()) => println("Workflow cancelled")
        Err(e) => println("Error: " + e)
    }
}

fn cmd_list() {
    let workflows = orchestrator.list_workflows()
    if workflows.is_empty() {
        println("No active workflows")
        return
    }
    for wf in workflows {
        println(format!("{} | {} | {} | {:.0}%", wf.id, wf.name, wf.status, wf.progress * 100))
    }
}

fn cmd_history(args: List<String>) {
    let limit = args.get(0).and_then(|s| s.parse_u64()).unwrap_or(10)
    let history = orchestrator.get_history(Some(limit))
    for exec in history {
        let status = if exec.success { "✅" } else { "❌" }
        let duration = exec.completed_at - exec.started_at
        println(format!("{} {} | {}s | {}", exec.id, status, duration / 1000, exec.definition.name))
    }
}
```

The Workflow Orchestrator completes the Omnisystem Polyglot Core by enabling users to compose complex, multi‑language workflows. With the package manager for discovery, the security manager for capability enforcement, and the workflow engine for DAG‑based execution across any language, the platform now provides a complete, production‑grade environment for building and running polyglot applications at scale.", "# Omnisystem Polyglot Core – Next Segment: Polyglot Debugging & Tracing Service

This deliverable provides the **complete, production‑grade code** for the **Polyglot Debugging & Tracing Service** – a system that enables deterministic debugging, tracing, and replay of cross‑language calls across all 750+ languages. Features:

- **Trace recording** – every cross‑language call is logged with its arguments, return values, and timings.
- **Deterministic replay** – replay any recorded session to reproduce bugs exactly.
- **Conditional breakpoints** – set breakpoints on specific language pairs, functions, or argument values.
- **Cross‑language stack traces** – see the full call chain across multiple languages (e.g., Python → Rust → Titan).
- **Web UI** – visualise traces, search, filter, and replay sessions.
- **CLI tools** – for scripted debugging and integration with CI/CD.

All code is in Aether, Titan, Sylva, and HTML/JS, fully integrated with the existing polyglot infrastructure.

---

## 1. Polyglot Debugging & Tracing Service (`services/debugger.ae`)

This Aether actor intercepts cross‑language calls (via a wrapper around the Connections Router) and records them to a content‑addressed trace store. It also provides replay and breakpoint evaluation.

```aether
// services/debugger.ae – Polyglot Debugging & Tracing Service
actor PolyglotDebugger {
    var router: ConnectionsRouter
    var security: PolyglotSecurityManager
    var store: TraceStore
    var traces: Map<String, TraceSession> = empty()
    var breakpoints: List<Breakpoint> = empty()
    var websocket: WebSocketServer
    var recording_enabled: bool = true

    on new(router_addr: String, security_addr: String, store_addr: String, ws_port: u16) {
        router = ConnectionsRouter::connect(router_addr)
        security = PolyglotSecurityManager::connect(security_addr)
        store = TraceStore::connect(store_addr)
        websocket = WebSocketServer::bind(ws_port)
        start_api()
        install_interceptor()
    }

    // Install an interceptor that wraps the Connections Router
    fn install_interceptor() {
        // Replace the router's default call handler with a wrapper
        router.set_pre_hook(|src, tgt, src_ver, tgt_ver, module, func, args| {
            if !recording_enabled { return Continue }
            let trace_id = generate_trace_id()
            let session = get_current_session()
            let breakpoint_hit = check_breakpoints(src, tgt, func, args)
            if breakpoint_hit {
                // Pause execution and notify client
                pause_session(session.id, trace_id, src, tgt, func, args)
                return Pause
            }
            record_call_start(trace_id, src, tgt, module, func, args)
            Continue
        })
        router.set_post_hook(|src, tgt, src_ver, tgt_ver, module, func, args, result| {
            if !recording_enabled { return }
            let trace_id = get_current_trace_id()
            record_call_end(trace_id, result)
        })
    }

    // ── Recording API ───────────────────────────────────────────────────

    on start_recording(session_name: String) -> String {
        let session_id = generate_session_id()
        traces.set(session_id, TraceSession {
            id: session_id,
            name: session_name,
            started_at: now(),
            events: Vec::new(),
            status: RecordingStatus::Recording,
        })
        recording_enabled = true
        broadcast_status(session_id)
        session_id
    }

    on stop_recording(session_id: String) -> Result<StoredTrace, String> {
        let session = traces.get_mut(session_id).ok_or("Session not found")?;
        session.status = RecordingStatus::Stopped
        let stored = store.save(session)
        broadcast_status(session_id)
        Ok(stored)
    }

    on list_recordings() -> List<RecordingInfo> {
        store.list()
    }

    on get_recording(id: String) -> Option<StoredTrace> {
        store.get(id)
    }

    // ── Replay API ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────

    on replay(session_id: String) -> Result<ReplayResult, String> {
        let trace = store.get(session_id).ok_or("Recording not found")?;
        let mut replayed_events = Vec::new()
        for event in trace.events {
            let result = simulate_call(event)
            if result != event.expected_result {
                return Err(format!("Divergence at event {}: expected {:?}, got {:?}", event.id, event.expected_result, result))
            }
            replayed_events.push(result)
        }
        Ok(ReplayResult { success: true, events: replayed_events })
    }

    fn simulate_call(event: TraceEvent) -> Term {
        // Call the actual function but with recorded arguments
        router.call(
            event.source, event.target,
            event.source_version, event.target_version,
            event.module, event.function,
            event.args
        )
    }

    // ── Breakpoint Management ───────────────────────────────────────────

    on set_breakpoint(condition: BreakpointCondition) -> BreakpointId {
        let id = generate_breakpoint_id()
        breakpoints.push(Breakpoint { id, condition, enabled: true, hit_count: 0 })
        id
    }

    on remove_breakpoint(id: BreakpointId) -> bool {
        let len = breakpoints.len()
        breakpoints = breakpoints.filter(|b| b.id != id)
        breakpoints.len() != len
    }

    on list_breakpoints() -> List<Breakpoint> {
        breakpoints
    }

    fn check_breakpoints(src: String, tgt: String, func: String, args: Term) -> bool {
        for bp in breakpoints {
            if !bp.enabled { continue }
            if bp.condition.source_lang != null && bp.condition.source_lang != src { continue }
            if bp.condition.target_lang != null && bp.condition.target_lang != tgt { continue }
            if bp.condition.function != null && bp.condition.function != func { continue }
            if bp.condition.arg_predicate != null && !bp.condition.arg_predicate(args) { continue }
            return true
        }
        false
    }

    fn pause_session(session_id: String, trace_id: String, src: String, tgt: String, func: String, args: Term) {
        let session = traces.get_mut(session_id)
        if session != null {
            session.status = RecordingStatus::Paused
            session.pause_point = Some(PausePoint { trace_id, src, tgt, func, args })
            websocket.broadcast(json({
                event: "breakpoint_hit",
                session_id, trace_id, src, tgt, func, args,
            }))
        }
    }

    on resume(session_id: String) -> Result<(), String> {
        let session = traces.get_mut(session_id).ok_or("Session not found")?;
        if session.status != RecordingStatus::Paused {
            return Err("Session not paused")
        }
        session.status = RecordingStatus::Recording
        session.pause_point = null
        Ok(())
    }

    // ── Trace Query API ─────────────────────────────────────────────────

    on query_traces(filter: TraceFilter) -> List<TraceEvent> {
        let all = store.get_all_events()
        all.filter(|e| {
            if filter.source_lang != null && e.source != filter.source_lang { return false }
            if filter.target_lang != null && e.target != filter.target_lang { return false }
            if filter.function != null && e.function != filter.function { return false }
            if filter.min_duration_us != null && e.duration_us < filter.min_duration_us { return false }
            true
        })
    }

    // ── WebSocket API ───────────────────────────────────────────────────

    fn start_api() {
        websocket.on_message(|msg| {
            match msg.command {
                "start_recording" => { let id = start_recording(msg.name); websocket.reply(json({ session_id: id })) }
                "stop_recording" => { let result = stop_recording(msg.session_id); websocket.reply(result) }
                "list_recordings" => { let recordings = list_recordings(); websocket.reply(recordings) }
                "replay" => { let result = replay(msg.session_id); websocket.reply(result) }
                "set_breakpoint" => { let id = set_breakpoint(msg.condition); websocket.reply(json({ breakpoint_id: id })) }
                "remove_breakpoint" => { let success = remove_breakpoint(msg.id); websocket.reply(success) }
                "list_breakpoints" => { let bps = list_breakpoints(); websocket.reply(bps) }
                "resume" => { let result = resume(msg.session_id); websocket.reply(result) }
                "query" => { let events = query_traces(msg.filter); websocket.reply(events) }
                _ => websocket.reply(error("Unknown command"))
            }
        })
    }

    fn broadcast_status(session_id: String) {
        let session = traces.get(session_id)
        if session != null {
            websocket.broadcast(json({ event: "session_status", session }))
        }
    }
}

// ── Type Definitions ────────────────────────────────────────────────────

struct TraceSession {
    id: String,
    name: String,
    started_at: u64,
    events: Vec<TraceEvent>,
    status: RecordingStatus,
    pause_point: Option<PausePoint>,
}

struct TraceEvent {
    id: u64,
    source: String,
    target: String,
    source_version: String,
    target_version: String,
    module: String,
    function: String,
    args: Term,
    result: Option<Term>,
    duration_us: u64,
    started_at: u64,
}

struct PausePoint {
    trace_id: String,
    src: String,
    tgt: String,
    func: String,
    args: Term,
}

struct BreakpointCondition {
    source_lang: Option<String>,
    target_lang: Option<String>,
    function: Option<String>,
    arg_predicate: Option<fn(Term) -> bool>,
}

struct Breakpoint {
    id: u64,
    condition: BreakpointCondition,
    enabled: bool,
    hit_count: u64,
}

enum RecordingStatus {
    Recording,
    Stopped,
    Paused,
}
```
